46 (g) Qualified Immunity, Defense, and Indemnification:
47 (1) The members, officers, executive director, employees, and representatives of
48 the Commission shall be immune from suit and liability, both personally and
49 in their official capacity, for any claim for damage to or loss of property or
50 personal injury or other civil liability caused by or arising out of any actual or
51 alleged act, error, or omission that occurred, or that the person against whom
Page 26 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 the claim is made had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within the
2 scope of Commission employment, duties, or responsibilities; provided that
3 nothing in this paragraph shall be construed to protect any such person from
4 suit or liability for any damage, loss, injury, or liability caused by the
5 intentional or willful or wanton misconduct of that person. The procurement
6 of insurance of any type by the Commission shall not in any way compromise
7 or limit the immunity granted hereunder.
8 (2) The Commission shall defend any member, officer, executive director,
9 employee, and representative of the Commission in any civil action seeking
10 to impose liability arising out of any actual or alleged act, error, or omission
11 that occurred within the scope of Commission employment, duties, or
12 responsibilities, or as determined by the Commission that the person against
13 whom the claim is made had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within
14 the scope of Commission employment, duties, or responsibilities; provided
15 that nothing herein shall be construed to prohibit that person from retaining
16 their own counsel at their own expense; and provided further, that the actual
17 or alleged act, error, or omission did not result from that person's intentional
18 or willful or wanton misconduct.
19 (3) The Commission shall indemnify and hold harmless any member, officer,
20 executive director, employee, and representative of the Commission for the
21 amount of any settlement or judgment obtained against that person arising out
22 of any actual or alleged act, error, or omission that occurred within the scope
23 of Commission employment, duties, or responsibilities, or that such person
24 had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within the scope of Commission
25 employment, duties, or responsibilities, provided that the actual or alleged act,
26 error, or omission did not result from the intentional or willful or wanton
27 misconduct of that person.
28 (4) Venue is proper and judicial proceedings by or against the Commission shall
29 be brought solely and exclusively in a court of competent jurisdiction where
30 the principal office of the Commission is located. The Commission may waive
31 venue and jurisdictional defenses in any proceedings as authorized by
32 Commission Rules.
33 (5) Nothing herein shall be construed as a limitation on the liability of any
34 Licensee for professional malpractice or misconduct, which shall be governed
35 solely by any other applicable State laws.
36 (6) Nothing herein shall be construed to designate the venue or jurisdiction to
37 bring actions for alleged acts of malpractice, professional misconduct,
38 negligence, or other such civil action pertaining to the practice of a PA. All
39 such matters shall be determined exclusively by State law other than this
40 Compact.
41 (7) Nothing in this Compact shall be interpreted to waive or otherwise abrogate a
42 Participating State's state action immunity or state action affirmative defense
43 with respect to antitrust claims under the Sherman Act, Clayton Act, or any
44 other State or federal antitrust or anticompetitive law or regulation.
45 (8) Nothing in this Compact shall be construed to be a waiver of sovereign
46 immunity by the Participating States or by the Commission.
47 "§ 90-270.207. Data System.
48 (a) The Commission shall provide for the development, maintenance, operation, and
49 utilization of a coordinated data and reporting system containing licensure, Adverse Action, and
50 the reporting of the existence of Significant Investigative Information on all licensed PAs and
51 applicants denied a License in Participating States.
House Bill 67-Second Edition Page 27

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (b) Notwithstanding any other State law to the contrary, a Participating State shall submit
2 a uniform data set to the Data System on all PAs to whom this Compact is applicable (utilizing
3 a unique identifier) as required by the Rules of the Commission, including:
4 (1) Identifying information;
5 (2) Licensure data;
6 (3) Adverse Actions against a License or Compact Privilege;
7 (4) Any denial of application for licensure, and the reason(s) for such denial
8 (excluding the reporting of any criminal history record information where
9 prohibited by law);
10 (5) The existence of Significant Investigative Information; and
11 (6) Other information that may facilitate the administration of this Compact, as
12 determined by the Rules of the Commission.
13 (c) Significant Investigative Information pertaining to a Licensee in any Participating
14 State shall only be available to other Participating States.
15 (d) The Commission shall promptly notify all Participating States of any Adverse Action
16 taken against a Licensee or an individual applying for a License that has been reported to it. This
17 Adverse Action information shall be available to any other Participating State.
18 (e) Participating States contributing information to the Data System may, in accordance
19 with State or federal law, designate information that may not be shared with the public without
20 the express permission of the contributing State. Notwithstanding any such designation, such
21 information shall be reported to the Commission through the Data System.
22 (f) Any information submitted to the Data System that is subsequently expunged
23 pursuant to federal law or the laws of the Participating State contributing the information shall
24 be removed from the Data System upon reporting of such by the Participating State to the
25 Commission.
26 (g) The records and information provided to a Participating State pursuant to this
27 Compact or through the Data System, when certified by the Commission or an agent thereof,
28 shall constitute the authenticated business records of the Commission and shall be entitled to any
29 associated hearsay exception in any relevant judicial, quasi-judicial, or administrative
30 proceedings in a Participating State.
31 "§ 90-270.208. Rulemaking.
32 (a) The Commission shall exercise its Rulemaking powers pursuant to the criteria set
33 forth in this section and the Rules adopted thereunder. Commission Rules shall become binding
34 as of the date specified by the Commission for each Rule.
35 (b) The Commission shall promulgate reasonable Rules in order to effectively and
36 efficiently implement and administer this Compact and achieve its purposes. A Commission Rule
37 shall be invalid and have not force or effect only if a court of competent jurisdiction holds that
38 the Rule is invalid because the Commission exercised its rulemaking authority in a manner that
39 is beyond the scope of the purposes of this Compact, or the powers granted hereunder, or based
40 upon another applicable standard of review.
41 (c) The Rules of the Commission shall have the force of law in each Participating State,
42 provided, however, that where the Rules of the Commission conflict with the laws of the
43 Participating State that establish the Medical Services a PA may perform in the Participating
44 State, as held by a court of competent jurisdiction, the Rules of the Commission shall be
45 ineffective in that State to the extent of the conflict. The Rules of the Commission shall not
46 modify or expand, in any way, the scope of practice of a PA as established by the laws of the
47 Participating State.
48 (d) If a majority of the legislatures of the Participating States rejects a Commission Rule,
49 by enactment of a statute or resolution in the same manner used to adopt this Compact within
50 four years of the date of adoption of the Rule, then such Rule shall have no further force and
51 effect in any Participating State or to any State applying to participate in the Compact.
Page 28 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (e) Commission Rules shall be adopted at a regular or special meeting of the
2 Commission.
3 (f) Prior to promulgation and adoption of a final Rule or Rules by the Commission, and
4 at least 30 days in advance of the meeting at which the Rule will be considered and voted upon,
5 the Commission shall file a Notice of Proposed Rulemaking:
6 (1) On the website of the Commission or other publicly accessible platform;
7 (2) To persons who have requested notice of the Commission's notices of
8 proposed rulemaking; and
9 (3) In such other way(s) as the Commission may by Rule specify.
10 (g) The Notice of Proposed Rulemaking shall include:
11 (1) The time, date, and location of the public hearing on the proposed Rule and
12 the proposed time, date, and location of the meeting in which the proposed
13 Rule will be considered and voted upon;
14 (2) The text of the proposed Rule and the reason for the proposed Rule;
15 (3) A request for comments on the proposed Rule from any interested person and
16 the date by which written comments must be received; and
17 (4) The manner in which interested persons may submit notice to the Commission
18 of their intention to attend the public hearing or provide any written
19 comments.
20 (h) Prior to adoption of a proposed Rule, the Commission shall allow persons to submit
21 written data, facts, opinions, and arguments, which shall be made available to the public.
22 (i) If the hearing is to be held via electronic means, the Commission shall publish the
23 mechanism for access to the electronic hearing.
24 (1) All persons wishing to be heard at the hearing shall as directed in the Notice
25 of Proposed Rulemaking, not less than five business days before the scheduled
26 date of the hearing, notify the Commission of their desire to appear and testify
27 at the hearing.
28 (2) Hearings shall be conducted in a manner providing each person who wishes
29 to comment a fair and reasonable opportunity to comment orally or in writing.
30 (3) All hearings shall be recorded. A copy of the recording and the written
31 comments, data, facts, opinions, and arguments received in response to the
32 proposed rulemaking shall be made available to a person upon request.
33 (4) Nothing in this section shall be construed as requiring a separate hearing on
34 each proposed Rule. Proposed Rules may be grouped for the convenience of
35 the Commission at hearings required by this section.
36 (j) Following the public hearing, the Commission shall consider all written and oral
37 comments timely received.
38 (k) The Commission shall, by majority vote of all delegates, take final action on the
39 proposed Rule and shall determine the effective date of the Rule, if adopted, based on the
40 Rulemaking record and the full text of the Rule.
41 (1) If adopted, the Rule shall be posted on the Commission's website.
42 (2) The Commission may adopt changes to the proposed Rule provided the
43 changes do not enlarge the original purpose of the proposed Rule.
44 (3) The Commission shall provide on its website an explanation of the reasons for
45 substantive changes made to the proposed Rule as well as reasons for
46 substantive changes not made that were recommended by commenters.
47 (4) The Commission shall determine a reasonable effective date for the Rule.
48 Except for an emergency as provided in subsection (l) of this section, the
49 effective date of the Rule shall be no sooner than 30 days after the Commission
50 issued the notice that it adopted the Rule.
House Bill 67-Second Edition Page 29

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (l) Upon determination that an emergency exists, the Commission may consider and
2 adopt an emergency Rule with 24 hours' prior notice, without the opportunity for comment, or
3 hearing, provided that the usual Rulemaking procedures provided in this Compact and in this
4 section shall be retroactively applied to the Rule as soon as reasonably possible, in no event later
5 than 90 days after the effective date of the Rule. For the purposes of this provision, an emergency
6 Rule is one that must be adopted immediately by the Commission in order to:
7 (1) Meet an imminent threat to public health, safety, or welfare;
8 (2) Prevent a loss of Commission or Participating State funds;
9 (3) Meet a deadline for the promulgation of a Commission Rule that is established
10 by federal law or Rule; or
11 (4) Protect public health and safety.
12 (m) The Commission or an authorized committee of the Commission may direct revisions
13 to a previously adopted Commission Rule for purposes of correcting typographical errors, errors
14 in format, errors in consistency, or grammatical errors. Public notice of any revisions shall be
15 posted on the website of the Commission. The revision shall be subject to challenge by any
16 person for a period of 30 days after posting. The revision may be challenged only on grounds
17 that the revision results in a material change to a Rule. A challenge shall be made as set forth in
18 the notice of revisions and delivered to the Commission prior to the end of the notice period. If
19 no challenge is made, the revision will take effect without further action. If the revision is
20 challenged, the revision may not take effect without the approval of the Commission.
21 (n) No Participating State's rulemaking requirements shall apply under this Compact.
22 "§ 90-270.209. Oversight, dispute resolution, and enforcement.
23 (a) Oversight:
24 (1) The executive and judicial branches of State government in each Participating
25 State shall enforce this Compact and take all actions necessary and appropriate
26 to implement the Compact.
27 (2) Venue is proper and judicial proceedings by or against the Commission shall
28 be brought solely and exclusively in a court of competent jurisdiction where
29 the principal office of the Commission is located. The Commission may waive
30 venue and jurisdictional defenses to the extent it adopts or consents to
31 participate in alternative dispute resolution proceedings. Nothing herein shall
32 affect or limit the selection or propriety of venue in any action against a
33 Licensee for professional malpractice, misconduct, or any such similar matter.
34 (3) The Commission shall be entitled to receive service of process in any
35 proceeding regarding the enforcement or interpretation of the Compact or the
36 Commission's Rules and shall have standing to intervene in such a proceeding
37 for all purposes. Failure to provide the Commission with service of process
38 shall render a judgment or order in such proceeding void as to the
39 Commission, this Compact, or Commission Rules.
40 (b) Default, Technical Assistance, and Termination:
41 (1) If the Commission determines that a Participating State has defaulted in the
42 performance of its obligations or responsibilities under this Compact or the
43 Commission Rules, the Commission shall provide written notice to the
44 defaulting State and other Participating States. The notice shall describe the
45 default, the proposed means of curing the default, and any other action that
46 the Commission may take and shall offer remedial training and specific
47 technical assistance regarding the default.
48 (2) If a State in default fails to cure the default, the defaulting State may be
49 terminated from this Compact upon an affirmative vote of a majority of the
50 delegates of the Participating States, and all rights, privileges, and benefits
51 conferred by this Compact upon such State may be terminated on the effective
Page 30 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 date of termination. A cure of the default does not relieve the offending State
2 of obligations or liabilities incurred during the period of default.
3 (3) Termination of participation in this Compact shall be imposed only after all
4 other means of securing compliance have been exhausted. Notice of intent to
5 suspend or terminate shall be given by the Commission to the governor, the
6 majority and minority leaders of the defaulting State's legislature, and to the
7 Licensing Board(s) of each of the Participating States.
8 (4) A State that has been terminated is responsible for all assessments,
9 obligations, and liabilities incurred through the effective date of termination,
10 including obligations that extend beyond the effective date of termination.
11 (5) The Commission shall not bear any costs related to a State that is found to be
12 in default or that has been terminated from this Compact, unless agreed upon
13 in writing between the Commission and the defaulting State.
14 (6) The defaulting State may appeal its termination from the Compact by the
15 Commission by petitioning the United States District Court for the District of
16 Columbia or the federal district where the Commission has its principal
17 offices. The prevailing member shall be awarded all costs of such litigation,
18 including reasonable attorneys' fees.
19 (7) Upon the termination of a State's participation in the Compact, the State shall
20 immediately provide notice to all Licensees within that State of such
21 termination:
22 a. Licensees who have been granted a Compact Privilege in that State
23 shall retain the Compact Privilege for 180 days following the effective
24 date of such termination.
25 b. Licensees who are licensed in that State who have been granted a
26 Compact Privilege in a Participating State shall retain the Compact
27 Privilege for 180 days unless the Licensee also has a Qualifying
28 License in a Participating State or obtains a Qualifying License in a
29 Participating State before the 180-day period ends, in which case the
30 Compact Privilege shall continue.
31 (c) Dispute Resolution:
32 (1) Upon request by a Participating State, the Commission shall attempt to resolve
33 disputes related to this Compact that arise among Participating States and
34 between Participating and non-Participating States.
35 (2) The Commission shall promulgate a Rule providing for both mediation and
36 binding dispute resolution for disputes as appropriate.
37 (d) Enforcement:
38 (1) The Commission, in the reasonable exercise of its discretion, shall enforce the
39 provisions of this Compact and Rules of the Commission.
40 (2) If compliance is not secured after all means to secure compliance have been
41 exhausted, by majority vote, the Commission may initiate legal action in the
42 United States District Court for the District of Columbia or the federal district
43 where the Commission has its principal offices, against a Participating State
44 in default to enforce compliance with the provisions of this Compact and the
45 Commission's promulgated Rules and bylaws. The relief sought may include
46 both injunctive relief and damages. In the event judicial enforcement is
47 necessary, the prevailing party shall be awarded all costs of such litigation,
48 including reasonable attorneys' fees.
49 (3) The remedies herein shall not be the exclusive remedies of the Commission.
50 The Commission may pursue any other remedies available under federal or
51 State law.
House Bill 67-Second Edition Page 31

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (e) Legal Action Against the Commission:
2 (1) A Participating State may initiate legal action against the Commission in the
3 United States District Court for the District of Columbia or the federal district
4 where the Commission has its principal offices to enforce compliance with the
5 provisions of the Compact and its Rules. The relief sought may include both
6 injunctive relief and damages. In the event judicial enforcement is necessary,
7 the prevailing party shall be awarded all costs of such litigation, including
8 reasonable attorneys' fees.
9 (2) No person other than a Participating State shall enforce this Compact against
10 the Commission.
11 "§ 90-270.210. Date of implementation of the PA Licensure Compact Commission.
12 (a) This Compact shall come into effect on the date on which this Compact statute is
13 enacted into law in the seventh Participating State.
14 (1) On or after the effective date of the Compact, the Commission shall convene
15 and review the enactment of each of the States that enacted the Compact prior
16 to the Commission convening ("Charter Participating States") to determine if
17 the statute enacted by each such Charter Participating State is materially
18 different than the Model Compact.
19 a. A Charter Participating State whose enactment is found to be
20 materially different from the Model Compact shall be entitled to the
21 default process set forth in G.S. 90-270.209(b).
22 b. If any Participating State later withdraws from the Compact or its
23 participation is terminated, the Commission shall remain in existence
24 and the Compact shall remain in effect even if the number of
25 Participating States should be less than seven. Participating States
26 enacting the Compact subsequent to the Commission convening shall
27 be subject to the process set forth in G.S. 90-270.206(c)(21) to
28 determine if their enactments are materially different from the Model
29 Compact and whether they qualify for participation in the Compact.
30 (2) Participating States enacting the Compact subsequent to the seven initial
31 Charter Participating States shall be subject to the process set forth in
32 G.S. 90-270.206(c)(21) to determine if their enactments are materially
33 different from the Model Compact and whether they qualify for participation
34 in the Compact.
35 (3) All actions taken for the benefit of the Commission or in furtherance of the
36 purposes of the administration of the Compact prior to the effective date of
37 the Compact or the Commission coming into existence shall be considered to
38 be actions of the Commission unless specifically repudiated by the
39 Commission.
40 (b) Any State that joins this Compact shall be subject to the Commission's Rules and
41 bylaws as they exist on the date on which this Compact becomes law in that State. Any Rule that
42 has been previously adopted by the Commission shall have the full force and effect of law on the
43 day this Compact becomes law in that State.
44 (c) Any Participating State may withdraw from this Compact by enacting a statute
45 repealing the same.
46 (1) A Participating State's withdrawal shall not take effect until 180 days after
47 enactment of the repealing statute. During this 180-day period, all Compact
48 Privileges that were in effect in the withdrawing State and were granted to
49 Licensees licensed in the withdrawing State shall remain in effect. If any
50 Licensee licensed in the withdrawing State is also licensed in another
51 Participating State or obtains a license in another Participating State within
Page 32 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 the 180 days, the Licensee's Compact Privileges in other Participating States
2 shall not be affected by the passage of the 180 days.
3 (2) Withdrawal shall not affect the continuing requirement of the State Licensing
4 Board(s) of the withdrawing State to comply with the investigative and
5 Adverse Action reporting requirements of this Compact prior to the effective
6 date of withdrawal.
7 (3) Upon the enactment of a statute withdrawing a State from this Compact, the
8 State shall immediately provide notice of such withdrawal to all Licensees
9 within that State. Such withdrawing State shall continue to recognize all
10 Licenses granted pursuant to this Compact for a minimum of 180 days after
11 the date of such notice of withdrawal.
12 (d) Nothing contained in this Compact shall be construed to invalidate or prevent any PA
13 licensure agreement or other cooperative arrangement between Participating States and between
14 a Participating State and non-Participating State that does not conflict with the provisions of this
15 Compact.
16 (e) This Compact may be amended by the Participating States. No amendment to this
17 Compact shall become effective and binding upon any Participating State until it is enacted
18 materially in the same manner into the laws of all Participating States as determined by the
19 Commission.
20 "§ 90-270.211. Construction and severability.
21 (a) This Compact and the Commission's rulemaking authority shall be liberally construed
22 so as to effectuate the purposes and the implementation and administration of the Compact.
23 Provisions of the Compact expressly authorizing or requiring the promulgation of Rules shall not
24 be construed to limit the Commission's rulemaking authority solely for those purposes.
25 (b) The provisions of this Compact shall be severable and if any phrase, clause, sentence,
26 or provision of this Compact is held by a court of competent jurisdiction to be contrary to the
27 constitution of any Participating State, a State seeking participation in the Compact, or of the
28 United States, or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance is
29 held to be unconstitutional by a court of competent jurisdiction, the validity of the remainder of
30 this Compact and the applicability thereof to any other government, agency, person, or
31 circumstance shall not be affected thereby.
32 (c) Notwithstanding subsection (b) of this section, the Commission may deny a State's
33 participation in the Compact or, in accordance with the requirements of G.S. 90-270.209(b),
34 terminate a Participating State's participation in the Compact, if it determines that a constitutional
35 requirement of a Participating State is, or would be with respect to a State seeking to participate
36 in the Compact, a material departure from the Compact. Otherwise, if this Compact shall be held
37 to be contrary to the constitution of any Participating State, the Compact shall remain in full force
38 and effect as to the remaining Participating States and in full force and effect as to the
39 Participating State affected as to all severable matters.
40 "§ 90-270.212. Binding effect of Compact.
41 (a) Nothing herein prevents the enforcement of any other law of a Participating State that
42 is not inconsistent with this Compact.
43 (b) Any laws in a Participating State in conflict with this Compact are superseded to the
44 extent of the conflict.
45 (c) All agreements between the Commission and the Participating States are binding in
46 accordance with their terms."

11 SECTION 5.2.(a) Article 3 of Chapter 58 of the General Statutes is amended by
12 adding a new section to read:
13 "§ 58-3-241. Healthcare services provided by pharmacists.
14 (a) The following definitions apply in this section:
15 (1) Healthcare provider. – Either of the following:
16 a. An individual who is licensed, certified, or otherwise authorized under
17 Chapter 90 of the General Statutes to provide healthcare services in
18 the ordinary course of business or practice of a profession or in an
19 approved education or training program.
20 b. A health care facility licensed under Chapter 131E or Chapter 122C of
21 the General Statutes and where healthcare services are provided to
22 patients.
23 (2) Healthcare services. – Any of the following health or medical procedures or
24 services rendered by a healthcare provider:
25 a. Testing, diagnosis, or treatment of a health condition, illness, injury,
26 or disease. This includes testing, diagnosis, or treatment rendered by a
27 pharmacist acting within the pharmacist's scope of practice.
28 b. Dispensing of drugs, medical devices, medical appliances, or medical
29 goods for the treatment of a health condition, illness, injury, or disease.
30 c. Administration of a vaccine or medication.
31 (3) Pharmacist. – An individual licensed to practice pharmacy under Article 4A
32 of Chapter 90 of the General Statutes or the relevant laws of another state.
33 (b) A health benefit plan offered by an insurer in this State shall cover healthcare services
34 provided by a pharmacist if all of the following conditions are met:
35 (1) The service or procedure was performed within the pharmacist's licensed
36 lawful scope of practice.
37 (2) The health benefit plan would have covered the service if the service or
38 procedure had been performed by another healthcare provider.
39 (c) The participation of a pharmacy in a drug benefit provider network of a health benefit
40 plan shall not satisfy any requirement that insurers offering health benefit plans include
41 pharmacists in medical benefit provider networks.
42 (d) An insurer shall accept a claim under this section regardless of whether it is submitted
43 by a pharmacist or a pharmacy submitting the claim on behalf of a pharmacist the pharmacy
44 employs or contracts with."
45 SECTION 5.2.(b) G.S. 58-3-230 is amended by adding a new subsection to read:

47 licensed under Article 4A of Chapter 90 of the General Statutes or the relevant laws of another
48 state to a contracted healthcare facility shall accept the credentialing for all pharmacists employed
49 by, or contracted with, those healthcare facilities."

18 shall remain in effect until the earlier of the date the permanent rules described in Section 5.3(b)
19 of this Part become effective or January 1, 2027.
20 SECTION 5.3.(b) No later than October 1, 2025, the North Carolina Medical Board
21 and the North Carolina Board of Pharmacy, in conjunction with the State Health Director, shall
22 adopt rules to implement the provisions of Section 5.1 of this Part. At a minimum, those rules
23 shall include:
24 (1) An approved course of treatment pharmacists may implement for influenza.
25 (2) Protocols for testing and treatment of influenza that balance patient safety with
26 ensuring access to care provided by pharmacists.
27 (3) If the Boards deem it appropriate, rules (i) limiting the number of times a
28 patient can be treated by a pharmacist in a given time span and (ii) creating an
29 audit mechanism to enforce those rules.
30 (4) Patient parameters necessitating referral to a primary, urgent, or emergency
31 care provider.
32 (5) Any other rules the Boards deem necessary.
33 SECTION 5.3.(c) Except as otherwise provided, this Part is effective when it
34 becomes law.

8 "§ 90-9.3. Requirements for licensure as a physician assistant.
9 (a) To be eligible for licensure as a physician assistant, an applicant shall submit proof
10 satisfactory to the Board that the applicant has met all of the following:
11 (1) The applicant has successfully completed an educational program for
12 physician assistants or surgeon assistants accredited by the Accreditation
13 Review Commission on Education for the Physician Assistant or its
14 predecessor or successor entities.
15 (2) The applicant has a current or previous certification issued by the National
16 Commission on Certification of Physician Assistants or its successor.
17 (3) The applicant is of good moral character.
18 (b) Before initiating practice of medical acts, tasks, or functions as a physician assistant,

25 SECTION 6.1.(c) Article 1 of Chapter 90 of the General Statutes is amended by
26 adding a new section to read:
27 "§ 90-9.3A. Requirements for team-based practice as a physician assistant.
28 (a) In order to practice as a team-based physician assistant, a physician assistant shall
29 meet all of the following conditions:
30 (1) Practice in team-based settings, as defined in G.S. 90-1.1(4d).
31 (2) Have more than 4,000 hours of clinical practice experience as a licensed
32 physician assistant and more than 1,000 hours of clinical practice experience
33 within the specific medical specialty of practice with a physician in that
34 specialty.
35 (3) Submit proof as the Board may deem satisfactory by rule that the individual
36 meets the requirements of subdivisions (1) and (2) of this subsection. The
37 Board may, by rule, require the physician assistant to comply with other
38 requirements or submit additional information the Board deems appropriate.
39 (b) Team-based physician assistants shall collaborate and consult with or refer to the
40 appropriate members of the health care team as required by the patient's condition and as
41 indicated by the education, experience, and competencies of the physician assistant and the
42 standard of care. The degree of collaboration must be determined by the practice which may
43 include decisions by the employer, group, hospital service, and the credentialing and privileging
44 systems of a licensed facility. The Board may adopt rules to establish requirements for the
45 determination and enforcement of collaboration, consultation, and referral. Team-based
46 physician assistants are responsible for the care they provide.
47 (c) Notwithstanding any other provision of this Chapter, a team-based physician assistant
48 practicing in a perioperative setting, including the provision of surgical or anesthesia-related
49 services, shall be supervised by a physician."

17 PART VII. PHARMACISTS COLLABORATIVE PRACTICE
18 SECTION 7.1.(a) G.S. 90-18(c)(3a) reads as rewritten:
19 "(3a) The provision of drug therapy management by a licensed pharmacist engaged
20 in the practice of pharmacy pursuant to an agreement that is physician,
21 pharmacist, patient, and disease specific when health care services by a
22 licensed pharmacist under a collaborative practice agreement with one or
23 more physicians shall be performed in accordance with rules and rules
24 developed by a joint subcommittee of the North Carolina Medical Board and
25 the North Carolina Board of Pharmacy and approved by both Boards. Drug
26 therapy management shall be defined as: (i) the implementation of
27 predetermined drug therapy which includes diagnosis and product selection
28 by the patient's physician; (ii) modification of prescribed drug dosages, dosage
29 forms, and dosage schedules; and (iii) ordering tests; (i), (ii), and (iii) shall be
30 pursuant to an agreement that is physician, pharmacist, patient, and disease
31 specific.For the purposes of this subdivision, "health care services" means
32 medical tasks, acts, or functions authorized through a written agreement by a
33 physician and delegated to a pharmacist for the purpose of providing drug
34 therapy, disease, or population health management for patients."
35 SECTION 7.1.(b) G.S. 90-18.4 reads as rewritten:
36 "§ 90-18.4. Limitations on clinical pharmacist practitioners.
37 (a) Any pharmacist who is approved under the provisions of G.S. 90-18(c)(3a) to perform
38 medical acts, tasks, and functions may use the title "clinical pharmacist practitioner". Any other
39 person who uses the title in any form or holds himself or herself out to be a clinical pharmacist
40 practitioner or to be so licensed shall be deemed to be in violation of this Article.
41 (b) Clinical pharmacist practitioners are authorized to implement predetermined drug
42 therapy, which includes diagnosis and product selection by the patient's physician, modify
43 prescribed drug dosages, dosage forms, and dosage schedules, and to order laboratory tests
44 pursuant to a drug therapy management agreement that is physician, pharmacist, patient, and
45 disease specific by physicians to provide health care services in accordance with
46 G.S. 90-18(c)(3a) and subsection (e) of this section under the following conditions:
47 (1) The North Carolina Medical Board and the North Carolina Board of Pharmacy
48 have adopted rules developed by a joint subcommittee governing the approval

50 management health care services with such limitations that the Boards

1 (2) The clinical pharmacist practitioner has current approval from both Boards.

4 written by the clinical pharmacist practitioner.

6 chemically dissimilar drug product by the pharmacist for the product
7 prescribed by the physician without the explicit consent of the physician and
8 includes a policy for periodic review by the physician of the drugs modified
9 pursuant to the agreement or changed with the consent of the physician.

11 established pharmacy and therapeutics committee or similar group that determines the
12 prescription drug formulary or other list of drugs to be utilized in the facility and determines
13 procedures to be followed when considering a drug for inclusion on the formulary and procedures
14 to acquire a nonformulary drug for a patient may order medications and tests under the following
15 conditions:
16 (1) The North Carolina Medical Board and the North Carolina Board of Pharmacy

20 (2) The clinical pharmacist practitioner has current approval from both Boards.
21 (3) The supervising physician has provided to the clinical pharmacist practitioner
22 written instructions for ordering, changing, or substituting drugs, or ordering
23 tests with provision for review of the order by the physician within a
24 reasonable time, as determined by the Boards, after the medication or tests are

31 safety.

34 the physician approved by the Boards as the supervisor of the clinical pharmacist practitioner and
35 the supervising physician shall be responsible for authorizing the prescription order.
36 (c2) Institutional and group practices may implement a site-specific, multi-provider
37 collaborative practice agreement for the care of their patients. The institution or group practice
38 must develop a policy for oversight, and the clinical pharmacist practitioners engaged in the

45 physicians engaging in collaborative practice:
46 (1) A clinical pharmacist practitioner shall have a site-specific supervising
47 physician.
48 (2) The supervising physician shall conduct periodic review and evaluation of the
49 health care services provided by the clinical pharmacist practitioner.
50 (3) A physician may collaborate with any number of clinical pharmacist
51 practitioners, but when acting as the supervising physician, they shall

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 supervise as many clinical pharmacist practitioners as the supervising

27 PART VIII. ALLEVIATE THE DANGERS OF SURGICAL SMOKE
28 SECTION 8.(a) Part 2 of Article 5 of Chapter 131E of the General Statutes is
29 amended by adding a new section to read:
30 "§ 131E-78.4. Hospital standards for surgical smoke evacuation.
31 (a) Definitions. – The following definitions apply in this section:
32 (1) Smoke evacuation/filtering system. – Stand-alone, portable equipment that
33 effectively captures, filters, and eliminates surgical smoke at the site of origin
34 before the smoke makes contact with the eyes or respiratory tracts of
35 occupants in the room. This equipment is not required to be interconnected to
36 the hospital surgical ventilation or medical gas system.
37 (2) Surgical smoke. – The gaseous by-product produced by energy-generating
38 devices, including surgical plume, smoke plume, bio-aerosols, laser-generated
39 airborne contaminants, or lung-damaging dust.
40 (b) Each hospital licensed under this Part shall adopt and implement policies that require
41 the use of a smoke evacuation/filtering system during any surgical procedure that is likely to
42 generate surgical smoke.
43 (c) Adverse Action. – The Department of Health and Human Services may take adverse
44 action against a hospital under G.S. 131E-78 for a violation of this section."
45 SECTION 8.(b) Part 4 of Article 6 of Chapter 131E of the General Statutes is
46 amended by adding a new section to read:
47 "§ 131E-147.2. Ambulatory surgical facility standards for surgical smoke evacuation.
48 (a) Definitions. – The following definitions apply in this section:
49 (1) Smoke evacuation/filtering system. – Equipment that effectively captures,
50 filters, and eliminates surgical smoke at the site of origin before the smoke
51 makes contact with the eyes or the respiratory tracts of occupants in the room.
House Bill 67-Second Edition Page 53

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 This equipment is not required to be interconnected to the ambulatory surgical
2 ventilation or medical gas system.
3 (2) Surgical smoke. – The gaseous by-product produced by energy-generating
4 devices, including surgical plume, smoke plume, bio-aerosols, laser-generated
5 airborne contaminants, or lung-damaging dust.
6 (b) Each ambulatory surgical facility licensed under this Part shall adopt and implement
7 policies that require the use of a smoke evacuation/filtering system during any surgical procedure
8 that is likely to generate surgical smoke.
9 (c) Adverse Action. – The Department of Health and Human Services may take adverse
10 action against an ambulatory surgical facility under G.S. 131E-148 for a violation of this section."
11 SECTION 8.(c) This Part becomes effective January 1, 2026.

13 PART IX. COMMUNITY COLLEGE BEHAVIORAL HEALTH WORKFORCE
14 ENHANCEMENT
15 SECTION 9.1.(a) Definitions. – For the purposes of this act, the following
16 definitions apply:
17 (1) Associate Professional (AP). – As defined in 10A NCAC 27G .0104(1).
18 (2) Commission. – Commission for Mental Health, Developmental Disabilities,
19 and Substance Abuse Services.
20 (3) Qualified Professional. – As defined in 10A NCAC 27G .0104(21).
21 (4) Qualified Substance Abuse Prevention Professional (QSAPP). – As defined
22 in 10A NCAC 27G .0104(22).
23 (5) Staff Definitions Rule. – 10A NCAC 27G .0104 (Staff Definitions).
24 SECTION 9.1.(b) Staff Definitions Rule. – Until the effective date of the revised
25 permanent rule that the Commission is required to adopt pursuant to subsection (e) of this section,
26 the Commission shall implement the Staff Definitions Rule as provided in subsections (c) and
27 (d) of this section.
28 SECTION 9.1.(c) Implementation. – With respect to the definitions of "Associate
29 Professional (AP)," "Qualified Professional," and "Qualified Substance Abuse Prevention
30 Professional (QSAPP)," the Staff Definitions Rule shall be implemented to provide the following
31 new qualification for each term, in addition to current qualifications, for each definition,
32 respectively:
33 (1) Associate Professional (AP). – May be a graduate of a community college
34 with an associate degree in a human services field with less than two years of
35 experience with the population served.
36 (2) Qualified Professional. – May be a graduate of a community college with an
37 associate degree in a human services field and has two years of full-time or
38 pre- or post-associate degree accumulated supervised mental health,
39 developmental disabilities, and substance abuse services experience with the
40 population served.
41 (3) Qualified Substance Abuse Prevention Professional (QSAPP). – May be a
42 graduate of a community college with an associate degree in the human
43 services field and has two years of full-time or pre- or post-associate degree
44 accumulated supervised experience in addictions and recovery prevention.
45 SECTION 9.1.(d) Additional Implementation. – With respect to the definition of
46 "Qualified Substance Abuse Prevention Professional (QSAPP)," the Staff Definitions Rule shall
47 be implemented to provide for accumulated supervised experience in substance abuse prevention
48 prior to the completion of a bachelor's degree to qualify for each pathway under 10A NCAC 27G
49 .0104(22)a. through d.
50 SECTION 9.1.(e) Additional Rulemaking Authority. – The Commission shall adopt
51 a rule to amend the Staff Definitions Rule consistent with subsections (c) and (d) of this section.
Page 54 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 Notwithstanding G.S. 150B-19(4), the rule adopted by the Commission pursuant to this section
2 shall be substantively identical to the provisions of subsections (c) and (d) of this section. Rules
3 adopted pursuant to this section are not subject to Part 3 of Article 2A of Chapter 150B of the
4 General Statutes. Rules adopted pursuant to this section shall become effective as provided in
5 G.S. 150B-21.3(b1), as though 10 or more written objections had been received as provided in

15 PART X. MARRIAGE AND FAMILY THERAPY LICENSURE REFORMS
16 SECTION 10.(a) G.S. 90-270.56 reads as rewritten:
17 "§ 90-270.56. Reciprocal licenses.
18 The Board may shall issue a license as a marriage and family therapist or a marriage and
19 family therapy associate by reciprocity to any person who applies for the license as prescribed
20 by the Board and who at all times during the application process:
21 (1) Has been licensed and actively practicing for five at least two continuous years
22 and is currently licensed as a marriage and family therapist or marriage and
23 family therapy associate in another state.
24 (2) Has an unrestricted license in good standing in the other state.
25 (3) Has no unresolved complaints in any jurisdiction.
26 (4) Has passed the National Marriage and Family Therapy
27 examination.examination or the clinical examination required by the licensing
28 board that regulates marriage and family therapy in the State of California."
29 SECTION 10.(b) G.S. 90-270.63 reads as rewritten:
30 "§ 90-270.63. Criminal history record checks of applicants for licensure as a marriage and
31 family therapist and a marriage and family therapy associate.

33 (1) Applicant. – A person applying for licensure as a licensed marriage and family

39 Board may adopt rules to implement the provisions of this act.

43 PART XI. LIMITATIONS ON AGREEMENTS WITH HEALTH CARE
44 PROFESSIONALS
45 SECTION 11.(a) Chapter 66 of the General Statutes is amended by adding a new
46 Article to read:
47 "Article 52.
48 "Limitations on Agreements With Health Care Professionals.
49 "§ 66-505. Definitions.
50 The following definitions apply in this Article:
House Bill 67-Second Edition Page 55

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (1) Health care professional. – An individual who is a licensed physician,
2 physician assistant, advanced practice registered nurse as defined by the North
3 Carolina Board of Nursing, or registered nurse.
4 (2) Hospital. – Any of the following:
5 a. A facility that has an organized medical staff and is designed, used,
6 and operated to provide health care, diagnostic and therapeutic
7 services, and continuous nursing care primarily to inpatients where
8 such care and services are rendered under the supervision and direction
9 of physicians licensed under Article 1 of Chapter 90 of the General
10 Statutes to two or more persons over a period in excess of 24 hours.
11 b. A facility designated by the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid
12 Services as a rural emergency hospital as defined under 42 C.F.R. §
13 485.502 or under section 125 of Division CC of the Consolidated
14 Appropriations Act of 2021, Public Law 116-260.
15 c. Any outpatient department, including a portion of a hospital operated
16 as an outpatient department, on or off of the hospital's main campus,
17 that is operated under the hospital's control or ownership and is
18 classified as a Business Occupancy by the Life Safety Code of the
19 National Fire Protection Association as referenced under 42 C.F.R. §
20 482.41.
21 d. Any hospital-owned medical practice.
22 (3) Medical staff bylaws. – A document that is required by a licensing,
23 accrediting, or regulatory body that governs the organization and operation of
24 a hospital's medical staff by defining the structure, roles, responsibilities, and
25 relationships between the medical staff, stakeholders, hospital administration,
26 and hospital governing board.
27 (4) Non-compete clause or clause. – An agreement that restricts a party from
28 engaging in certain types of employment or business activities for a specified
29 period of time within a specified geographic area.
30 (5) Nondisclosure agreement. – An agreement that restricts the ability of a party
31 to disclose information.
32 "§ 66-506. Nondisclosure agreements limited.
33 (a) Any nondisclosure agreement entered into with a health care professional must
34 explicitly state that it does not restrict the health care professional from reporting safety concerns,
35 ethical violations, or illegal activities.
36 (b) No health care professional may be required to enter into a nondisclosure agreement
37 that would do any of the following:
38 (1) Prevent the health care professional from discussing patient safety concerns
39 with licensing agencies, accrediting bodies, or other regulatory or oversight
40 entities.
41 (2) Restrict the health care professional's ability to report to the appropriate
42 authorities violations of law, medical ethics, or medical staff bylaws.
43 "§ 66-507. Certain non-compete clauses prohibited.
44 An employment contract for a health care professional employed by a hospital shall not
45 contain a non-compete clause.
46 "§ 66-508. Provision of information.
47 Any policy, nondisclosure agreement, non-compete clause, medical staff bylaw, or any other
48 type of contractual agreement with a health care professional shall not prohibit the provision of
49 new practice information upon request by a patient and, if available, the recipient of that request
50 shall provide that information upon that request.
51 § 66-509. Remedies.
Page 56 House Bill 67-Second Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (a) A nondisclosure agreement or non-compete clause that violates this Article is void
2 and unenforceable.
3 (b) A health care professional who prevails in an action under this Article challenging the
4 enforceability of a nondisclosure agreement or non-compete clause is entitled to damages plus
5 reasonable attorneys' fees and costs.
6 SECTION 11.(b) The North Carolina Medical Board may adopt rules to implement
7 the provisions of this Part that pertain to physicians and physician assistants.
8 SECTION 11.(c) The North Carolina Board of Nursing may adopt rules to
9 implement the provisions of this Part that pertain to advanced practice registered nurses and
10 registered nurses.
11 SECTION 11.(d) This Part is effective October 1, 2025, and applies to contracts
12 entered into, modified, or renewed on or after that date.
13
14 PART XII. EFFECTIVE DATE
15 SECTION 12. Except as otherwise provided, this act is effective when it becomes
16 law.
